    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_89a624c5-bb41-4580-9ad0-7dacaf09754e'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10424736012123396621">All is not well in the Letherii Empire. Rhulad Sengar, the Emperor of a Thousand Deaths, spirals into madness, surrounded by sycophants and agents of his Machiavellian chancellor, while the Letherii secret police conduct a campaign of terror against its own people. The Errant, once a farseeing god, is suddenly blind to the future. Conspiracies seethe throughout the palace,</span>
  <span id="freeText10424736012123396621" style="display:none">All is not well in the Letherii Empire. Rhulad Sengar, the Emperor of a Thousand Deaths, spirals into madness, surrounded by sycophants and agents of his Machiavellian chancellor, while the Letherii secret police conduct a campaign of terror against its own people. The Errant, once a farseeing god, is suddenly blind to the future. Conspiracies seethe throughout the palace, as the empire - driven by the corrupt and self-interested - edges ever-closer to all-out war with the neighbouring kingdoms. And the great Edur fleet - its warriors selected from countless peoples - draws ever closer. Amongst them are Karsa Orlong and Icarium Lifestealer - each destined to cross blades with the emperor himself. That yet more blood is to be spilled is inevitable... Against this backdrop, a band of fugitives seek a way out of the empire, but one of them, Fear Sengar must find the soul of Scabandari Bloodeye. It is his hope that it might help halt the Tiste Edur, and so save his brother, the emperor. Yet, travelling with them is Scabandari's most ancient foe: Silchas Ruin, brother of Anomander Rake. And his motives are anything but certain - for the wounds he carries on his back, made by the blades of Scabandari, are still fresh. Fate decrees that there is to be a reckoning, for such bloodshed cannot go unanswered - and it will be a reckoning on an unimaginable scale...<br /><br /><br />A brutal, harrowing novel of war, intrigue and dark, uncontrollable magic, this is epic fantasy at its most imaginative, storytelling at its most thrilling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10424736012123396621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1114759-can-someone-explain-the-dialogue-between"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Can someone explain the dialogue between the Errant and the Feather Witch and their entire sub-plot? I could never figure out the motivations behind the witch taking his eye, and whatever happened between those two consequently.<br /><br />Also, what happened to fener eventually? Did I miss something after his only appearance in the book?<br /><br />The God related plot-lines are terribly convoluted. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7636901-virgiliu"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1328524738i/7636901._UY100_CR6,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7636901-virgiliu">Virgiliu</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Yeah, the whole Fether Witch plot is a variation of the inversion of control between god and followers theme. Same as with D'rek and her followers in <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Yeah, the whole Fether Witch plot is a variation of the inversion of control between god and followers theme. Same as with D'rek and her followers in The Bonehunters, The Errant decides to free himself by eliminating his priesthood (in this case, Feather Witch).<br /><br />We're gonna see what happens with the Boar of Summer. First time we saw him was in Dead House Gates and his arc comes to a conclusion at the end of the series.<br /><a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div id="review_1830298683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830298683" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830298683?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765348845" href="/book/show/5878388-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830298683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4767228743901248226"><b>The Reaper used his scythe to chop onions in an attempt to bring tears to my eyes. Unfortunately, he didn’t succeed.</b><br/><br/>By this point of the series, I think it’s safe to say now that <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> will never break my heart the way it did a lot of readers. People always told me that Erikson was more brutal towards his characters more than George R. R. Martin or all the conclusion of his books will leave my soul crushed; I strongly disagree with these as I found none of the books in the s</span>
  <span id="freeText4767228743901248226" style="display:none"><b>The Reaper used his scythe to chop onions in an attempt to bring tears to my eyes. Unfortunately, he didn’t succeed.</b><br><br>By this point of the series, I think it’s safe to say now that <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> will never break my heart the way it did a lot of readers. People always told me that Erikson was more brutal towards his characters more than George R. R. Martin or all the conclusion of his books will leave my soul crushed; I strongly disagree with these as I found none of the books in the series so far to ever move me to the point of making my soul crushed or on the brink of tears. This series is amazing in many other aspects but for characterizations (which is the most important aspect of any story for me), in my opinion there are several authors who did it better. <br><br>Before you raise your pitchfork, let me emphasize that the reason behind this comes down to the simple fact that Erikson spread out his characterizations to way too many characters, and for what it’s worth, what he did with more than hundreds of characters were incredible. However, because there were too many characters POV, I was never invested in the majority of the characters as much as I did with some of my beloved series that has a normal amount (let’s say one until more or less thirty POV throughout the series) of characters to follow. I was super happy with what Erikson did in <i>The Bonehunter</i>s; he introduced a relatively few new characters (many awesome ones at that too) and we get to follow mostly characters that we’re familiar with. In here though? The drammatis personae shot up to at least 150 characters and we’re forced to read so many completely uninteresting new characters POV; more info on this later.<br><br><i>Reaper’s Gale</i>, the seventh book in the <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> series brings the plot back to Letherii, the location where the story of <i>Midnight Tides</i> (one of my favorite books in the series) took place in. I won’t be talking about the plot at all, this is the seventh book already. My introductory paragraph and my rating should give you an indication that I have mixed feelings about this installment. Trust me that I honestly wish I could give this book 5 stars but doing that would be a lie. Here’s the thing, <i>Reaper’s Gale</i> provided me some scenes that could be included into one of the best scenes from the series, but unfortunately it also provided me with some of the worst and boring experience in the series.<br><br>The first 40% (twelve chapters) of the book were quite a mess for me to read. Erikson focused the story on mostly new characters I simply don’t care about. This is the seventh book already for god sake, and after reading the book, some of the new characters felt almost as if they were there just for the sake of making this book longer or unnecessarily more complex than it should be. Usually, I don’t mind Erikson introducing new characters, that’s what he always did with each installment. However, Erikson was capable of giving distinct voices to his characters and that very important ability was lost to me in this installment. Most of the new characters sounded almost completely the same and their POV became uninteresting to read. One of the newest character, Redmask, was one of the most disappointing character storylines within the series so far. I genuinely laughed because the conclusion of his story was so damn ridiculous, unsatisfying, and pointless; it made me think “what was the point of me reading his story? This could’ve been almost entirely skipped and my experience reading this book will most likely get better.”<br><br>Although Redmask was one of the worst and—for now—pointless characters in the series so far, Erikson also included one new side character that I consider one of the best character Erikson ever wrote; his name is Beak. Let me get this straight, Beak didn’t get a lot of POV for us to read but just with a few POV chapters, Erikson managed to make sure his characteristics, background, motivation, ability, were all fleshed out. His characterization was so damn incredible that even simple line like this passage down below holds a tremendous amount of impact.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Yes sir. You’ll see. Everyone will because you’re all my friends and friends are important. The most important thing in the world. And I’ll show you.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I’ll be honest, the book was barely a 3 stars read for me until the last 20% of the book happened. Although the road to get to the last 20% was full of up and down for me, it still felt rewarding to reach the climax sequences because the last three chapters of the book offer some scenes that would definitely be considered as some of the most memorable scenes within the series. Friendship, loyalty, destruction, flashes of light, bloody duels, and sorcery conflagration shine in the last 20%. The climax sequences of the book were executed magnificently and all the manipulation, scheming, and politics within Letheras was still as good as ever; I just wish there would be more of them just like how it was in <i>Midnight Tides.</i><br><br><b>Picture: One of the interior artworks in the Subterranean edition by Tommy Arnold</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536494638i/26277039._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The last great things about this book that I can say without spoilers would be the return of my favorite duo, and of course getting to see the continuation to the Emperor of a Thousand Deaths plotline. Lastly, as always, every time the story put me in the POV of familiar characters from the previous installments, I became completely enthralled and immersed in the story.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Why, without a sense of humour, you are blind to so much in the world. To human nature. To the absurdity of so much that we say and do.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Despite a lot of setbacks within this installment and my personal opinion that this is currently the second weakest book of the series so far, <i>Reaper’s Gale</i> was still overall a great book. There’s probably no chance that the series will follow characters we’re familiar with in the last three books of the series, but I’m still hopeful that Erikson will somehow get the story back on the track of greatness like he did with the third, fifth, and sixth installment of the series.<br><br><b>You can order the book <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780553813166/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE!</a></u></b><br><br><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2018/09/09/reapers-gale/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4767228743901248226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1204744990" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204744990" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204744990?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781409083283" href="/book/show/13482380-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=dr-reading-challenge">dr-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204744990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18298696865225535146"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>I will not be the first to extoll the astounding breadth and depth of the Malazan world with its extensive history, a multitude of races, richly diverse cultures and a huge cast of characters. I may also not be the first to admit how lost I sometimes feel, wandering through this labyrinth of intricate worldbuilding.<br/><br/><i>Reaper's Gale</i> was the first volume in the <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> which, much to my delight, continued directly from the previous book. There was no whiplash from the sud</span>
  <span id="freeText18298696865225535146" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br><br>I will not be the first to extoll the astounding breadth and depth of the Malazan world with its extensive history, a multitude of races, richly diverse cultures and a huge cast of characters. I may also not be the first to admit how lost I sometimes feel, wandering through this labyrinth of intricate worldbuilding.<br><br><i>Reaper's Gale</i> was the first volume in the <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> which, much to my delight, continued directly from the previous book. There was no whiplash from the sudden change in plot lines from one book to the other in the past six books. Almost all the subplots from the previous novels led into this one with a lot of known main characters showing up one way or another, all of which descended upon the Letherii Empire.<br><br>The very same empire we visited in the fifth book, one which was corrupted to the core, enthralled by coin and in the grip of a financial meltdown, engineered by a genius who was hell-bent on breaking the chains the wealthy few held over the larger citizenry of Letheras. Within this story lies a compelling commentary on the evil of greed and power perpetrated by the garnering of wealth.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"Where is the virtue in any of it? Is possession a virtue? Is a lifetime working for some rich toad a virtue? Is loyal employment in some merchant house a virtue? Loyal to what? To whom? Oh, have they paid for that loyalty with a hundred docks a week? Like any other commodity? But then, which version is truer - the virtue of self-serving acquisitiveness or the virtue of loyalty to one's employer?"</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br>As grimdark served to portray the greyness of humanity, many of the characters we have come across do fit that description very well. These are not bad people, but those who were driven to dubious choices and actions arising from circumstances, rightly or wrongly. However, arising from this aspect of greed for coin and power was where I truly found blackness. Here we find despicable characters which were borne from the vicious cycle of money ever rising to the top, in a society where the rich gets richer, and the poor get poorer. In this respect, Reaper's Gale was one of the darker instalments in this series thus far.<br><br>In spite of the many familiar faces, the reader was yet again greeted by another cast of new names, tribes and cultures, such as the Awl and the Shake. The Malazan marines were made up of the most diverse group of hardened soldiers, with nicknames which were either quite apt or hilarious or sometimes both. The way in which Erikson switched points-of-view between a significant number of the Malazan marines was masterful. Instead of the more common way of seeing a battle or fight sequence through the eyes of a few main characters, Erikson employed a method where we moved from one squad to another, usually in quick succession, through the individual perspectives of a large cast of characters. This in effect created both a more immersive experience as well as getting into the heads of soldiers as they face possible death. It can also get confusing when names you've never seen before suddenly popped up and you found yourself introduced to the sergeant of the 5th Squad, 10th Company, etc.<br><br>As compared to most of the earlier ones, the numerous threads and plotlines in this book did appear to be more interconnected. Perhaps this could be due to the larger picture being more apparent as the tale slowly progressed towards its denouement. It also goes without saying that each <i>Malazan Book of The Fallen</i> had always been emotionally powerful, and this volume was possibly one of the most at this point of the series.<br><br><b>Subterranean Press Limited Edition Cover</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493816587i/22655592._SY540_.jpg" width="363" height="549" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As much as I would love to gush about the characters again, I feel that I've reached a point in this series where I should refrain from saying too much. Safe to say that this instalment had some of the most awesome and badass characters reappearing and doing what they do best. Aside from the Malazan marines, we have <i>the</i> walking legend, a mage who is much more than what he seemed, my favourite duo of the series and <i>that</i> superlative warrior from a gigantic race thought long extinct.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"Not overconfident. Not indifferent. Not even contemptuous. No easy explanations for this Toblakai warrior. He would be within himself, entirely within himself, until it was time.... to witness."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br>My initial impression of the finale herein was that it was strangely anticlimactic after the build-up which started all the way from the previous book. Upon rereading this though, I appreciated that what was needed to be told for now was wrapped up as satisfactorily as possible. The tale hence will continue.<br><br><i>
  <b>"So in these our last days<br>The end of what we see is inside<br>Where it all began and begins never again<br>A moment's reprieve, then darkness falls."</b>
</i><br><br><strong>You can purchase the book from <u><a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Reapers-Gale-Steven-Erikson/9780553813166/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free Shipping)</a></u>.</strong><br><br><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-1E7" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and my other reviews at <a href="http://novelnotions.net/category/book-reviews/tss-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions.</a></i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18298696865225535146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2042416279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2042416279" />
    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2042416279?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553813166" href="/book/show/2893217-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=grim-dark">grim-dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2042416279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9286853576134593269"><b>Full review now up!</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Warning: Minor spoilers from earlier books in the series!</u>
</b><br/><br/>I have been reading this series for a while now. Right at 5 months to be exact. And I find myself taking more and more time in between each book. Whether to reflect on what I have read or just needing a break I’m not quite sure. These books are huge and contain more information in one volume that some do in an entire series.<br/> <br/><i>Reapers Gale</i> was the largest book in the <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> I have yet to read. After</span>
  <span id="freeText9286853576134593269" style="display:none"><b>Full review now up!</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Warning: Minor spoilers from earlier books in the series!</u>
</b><br /><br />I have been reading this series for a while now. Right at 5 months to be exact. And I find myself taking more and more time in between each book. Whether to reflect on what I have read or just needing a break I’m not quite sure. These books are huge and contain more information in one volume that some do in an entire series.<br /> <br /><i>Reapers Gale</i> was the largest book in the <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i> I have yet to read. After 3 weeks and adult life getting in the way several times I finally finished it. I feel like I should mark this off my bucket list. <br /><br />It has been several years since the events of <i>Midnight Tides</i>, and the people of Lether have become accustomed to the Tist Edur rule. The Emperor of a Thousand Deaths, Rhulad Sengar, has defeated every champion he has faced and his reign goes unchallenged….or does it. Others with power seek to find a way to weed out the Edur ruler and his kind, and the return of the Edur fleet brings with it two new champions that are unlike anything the Emperor has yet to face.<br /> <br />Meanwhile, the Bonehunters have payback in mind. They have tracked the Edur fleet to the continent of Lether and intend to rid the Letheri people of their oppressive rulers. But what they expect and what they find may have them changing their tactics in order to make it out alive. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘It is the curse of leaders to believe they can truly change the world.’</i>
</b><br /><br />As with all of the Malazan books <i>Reapers Gale</i> has many different story arcs that are each enjoyable in their own way. I wouldn’t say it was as action packed as <i>The Bonehunters</i>, but it wasn’t lacking in enjoyment either. Erikson’s writing can leave you wandering what the hell you just read at times, but his humor is spot on and I found myself laughing out loud at times.<br /> <br />While I enjoy the humor in these books, the heartbreak seems to outweigh anything. Maybe it’s due to most of the heartbreak coming near the end. All of the books don’t end this way. At least not for me, but I guess it depends on what characters you get attached to. This was one of those books. Erikson has a way of just breaking your heart through his descriptions of these scenes and the people they effect.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘We give voice to our sorrow, to our loss. In discovering what it is to die, we have been cast out from the world. In discovering beauty, we were made ugly.’</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Reapers Gale</i> probably won’t make it to my top 3 of the Malazan books, but that doesn’t mean it’s not 5 star material. Everyone that reads this series has their favorites, and of course I have my own. If I had one problem with this book it was that it felt a little drawn out, but that isn’t going to lower my rating. Too many pros for one minor con to change my opinion. Erikson has his descriptive and at times a little too intellectual for me writing style, but I love it. I can’t recommend this series enough!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘The end….is never what you imagine. Be comforted by that my friends.’</i>
</b><br /><br />5 stars *****</span>
  <a data-text-id="9286853576134593269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2309354028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2309354028" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2309354028?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781409083283" href="/book/show/13482380-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2309354028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8798152272927636164"><b>
  <i><br/>When stone is water, time is ice.<br/> When all is frozen in place fates rain down in fell torrent.<br/>My face revealed, in this stone that is water.<br/> The ripples locked hard to its shape a countenance passing strange.<br/>Ages will hide when stone is water.<br/> Cycles bound in these depths are flawed illusions breaking the stream.<br/>When stone is water, time is ice.<br/> When all is frozen in place our lives are stones in the torrent.<br/>And we rain down, rain down<br/> like water on stone<br/> with every strike of the hand.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I thou</span>
  <span id="freeText8798152272927636164" style="display:none"><b>
  <i><br />When stone is water, time is ice.<br /> When all is frozen in place fates rain down in fell torrent.<br />My face revealed, in this stone that is water.<br /> The ripples locked hard to its shape a countenance passing strange.<br />Ages will hide when stone is water.<br /> Cycles bound in these depths are flawed illusions breaking the stream.<br />When stone is water, time is ice.<br /> When all is frozen in place our lives are stones in the torrent.<br />And we rain down, rain down<br /> like water on stone<br /> with every strike of the hand.</i>
</b><br /><br />I thought no book in this series would break my heart as much as MoI, how wrong I was, this book is more heart-breaking, so much deaths and suffering. Despite this being heart-breaking its now my number one favourite in this series, there is basically nothing I hate in this book. It was fast paced, has way more characters than the previous books, this book features the Malazans, Tiste Edur, Letherris and a host of others. I also enjoy the representations in this book. Religion, race, simpletons, feminism etc. Despite this series being an epic fantasy it is still relatable, I think we humans don't really change no matter the world, time or century.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Pain was not to be embraced. Chaos was anathema to a mortal body. It ruined the flesh because it did not belong there. There was no exaltation in self-destruction.</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />The only thing am going to say about the world building is that it gets better, its explicit and in-depth. The book is written in third person multiple POVs of like a million characters, I enjoy the switch between the characters, but I can’t help wishing my favourites have more POVs.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>In discovering what it is to die, we have been cast out from the world.<br />In discovering beauty, we were made ugly.<br />We do not suffer in the manner that beasts suffer – for they surely do. We suffer with the memory of how it was before suffering came, and this deepens the wound, this tears open the pain. There is no beast that can match our anguish.</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>Characters and Plot</u><br />My favourite aspect in this book. <i> If you’ve yet to read the previous book, this part contains minor spoilers, cause I’ll mention the characters</i><br /><br /><b>The Malazans</b><br />The bonehunters to be more precise, The surviving ones which include Tavore, Keneb, Blistig, Lastora Yil and the squads. Fiddler, Gesler, Hellian, Urb and their squads are now in Letherri after the incident in Bonehunters, they plan to hunt the Edurs but things never go as planned. Some other new Bonehunters are introduced and I already have two favourites, Beak and Skulldeath.<br /><br /><b>The Letherris</b><br />My beloved Tehol and Bugg, are still continuing in their plot to bring down the economy, but the ruling class are now aware that someone is messing with the economy. Ublala Pung is also in this, he all but move in with Tehol. <br /><br />Despite the fact that my review is extremely lengthy, I just have to add this conversation.<br /><b>
  <i>'Good thinking, Ublala. Now, stay close to me. I am, after all, a master of this thieving skulduggery.'<br />'Really? But Bugg said—'<br />'What? What did my miserable manservant say? About me? Behind my back?'<br />Ublala shrugged. 'Lots of things. I mean, nothing. Oh, you misheard me, Tehol.<br />They heard the scuff of boots from the street, then a loud voice: 'There! Who's skulking in that alley?'<br />Ublala flinched down. 'How did he know?'<br />'We better run!'<br />They bolted.</i>
</b><br />And when he got home...<br /><b>
  <i>'They will be on the lookout now,' Bugg observed, 'for a man wearing a blanket.'<br />'Well,' Tehol retorted, 'there must be plenty of those, right?'<br />There was no immediate reply.<br />'There must be,' Tehol insisted, a little wildly even to his own ears. He hastened on in a more reasonable tone. 'The ever growing divide between the rich and the poor and all that. Why, blankets are the new fashion among the destitute. I'm sure</i>
</b><br /><br />We still have Shurq Elalle who is now a pirate and some new characters but my fav among the new ones is Janath, I all but loathe the rest. Seren Pedac is still recovering from the incidents that happened in MT, even at that she still manage to guide them. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She and Trull got reunited, got married then he died, she was pregnant for him when he died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>The Edurs</b><br />Need I mention my favourite is Trull, He is just too good, they just don’t deserve him, the rest could go and die, except Fear, I grew to like him in this, he is not that bad, he is just a one track mind guy, so all what happened was just too much for him. I just can’t decide whether I hate or pity Rhulad, he should just remain dead.<br /><br /><b>The Others</b><br />Karsa Orlong, Samar Dev, Icarium and Taralack are all in Letherri, amongst the champions that is to duel with Rhulad to the death. I really enjoy the character development of them except Taralack that I loathe cause of what he is doing to Icarium.<br /><br />Toc Anaster finally made an appearance, as always I enjoyed his PoV, and adore his character development.<br />Tool, Kilava and Hetan are also in this, even though it was just towards the ending.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ They were too late and came just when Toc died, also Tool and Hetan are now married <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Something major happened to Onrack <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ he is now flesh and blood and has a son <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Udinaas the pessimist, I can’t even hate him, the man has being through so much. I really love how he handled things with Rud Elalle, I was scared he might ruin things. Rud Elalle is now among my favourite characters.<br /><br />Nimander Golit is so not what I expected him to be, I thought he would be a bit like his father, but no he is nothing like Anomander. He is so broken and indifferent, I hope things gets better for him.<br /><br />Finally Silchas Ruin, the albino Tiste Andii, despite him being cruel I still like him, I love that he kept his promise to the Azath.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8798152272927636164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1975353232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1975353232" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1975353232?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1975353232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3988868106272593397">This was another excellent edition in Steven Erikson's Malazan Book of the Fallen series. It probably failed to hit the heights of the very best Malazan books I've read but I'd still rate it above Deadhouse Gates in terms of overall quality. <br/><br/>I loved the fact that we returned to the continent of Letheras for this story. I was a massive fan of the fourth book and its characters so it was great to return there to witness the aftermath of the Edur occupation of Letheras. The Edur and Letharii cultur</span>
  <span id="freeText3988868106272593397" style="display:none">This was another excellent edition in Steven Erikson's Malazan Book of the Fallen series. It probably failed to hit the heights of the very best Malazan books I've read but I'd still rate it above Deadhouse Gates in terms of overall quality. <br /><br />I loved the fact that we returned to the continent of Letheras for this story. I was a massive fan of the fourth book and its characters so it was great to return there to witness the aftermath of the Edur occupation of Letheras. The Edur and Letharii cultures were so different and it was fun to see how they combined to give us the government we found in this story. <br /><br />The other big plus for this Malazan instalment was that it featured a ton of the very best characters. As well as the stars from Midnight Tides we got the Bonehunters pitching up here after their flight from Malaz City at the end of the last book. We also got other big hitters like Karsa, Icarium, Toc, Onrack, and Quick Ben! <br /><br />The stand-out stars for me were probably Karsa, Quick Ben, and the duo of Tehol and Bugg. Pretty much all the scenes involving those guys were exciting and compelling. Honourable mention goes to Beak. His story arc was the strongest one of the entire book for me. <br /><br />The strongest aspects of the book for me was the overall way the story developed and the way Erikson depicted the way the new Edur occupied Letheras functioned. I did not love the scenes involving Tanal Yathvanar, they were mostly a bit brutal for my liking, but on the whole I loved the stuff we got from the Liberty Consort and the Patriotists. I'll not say too much about the overall direction of the story but I did love how it played out. I suspected Erikson was going to lean in this direction from the early tone of the story but I definitely did not expect him to go all out in it! I was surprised but strangely happy with the way things played out in the end parts of this story. <br /><br />Another strong point in this books favour was Erikson's depictions of war and battle. He is truly fantastic at showing the horrors of war and of how there is always two sides to every story. Even the supposed "good guys" are often painted in a critical light by Erikson. <br /><br />In terms of flaws I felt like Erikson let his tendency to philosophise overshadow the story on a few occasions. I've never felt like that in the previous instalments but this time around I did feel a few scenes served no other story function other than to have the characters act as mouthpieces for a few of Erikson's observations. He is usually a bit smoother than that! I was also not a giant fan of the whole Redmask story arc. It felt a bit pointless and every character who was caught up in that story arc ended up floundering a bit(Even a legend like Toc!). I hope the arc has some sort of future payoff. <br /><br />Rating: 4.5 stars. I rounded down. I feel a bit bad for rating this one less than 5 stars. Compared to most books it would be an easy 5 stars but compared to some of the other Malazan books in this series I just felt like this one was a tiny bit below their high standard. <br /><br />Audio Note: Michael Page does a good job with the audio of this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3988868106272593397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2286325053" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2286325053" />
    <a title="Stefan Bach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach"><img alt="Stefan Bach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603215087p2/24053713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2286325053?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Bach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Bach" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach">Stefan Bach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11532022-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2286325053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13216302451526824573"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Never mind the truth. The past is what I say it is. <br/>That is the freedom of teaching the ignorant."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>You know, we spend our lives in ordinary mundane affairs. We behave in a mundane way, we dress in a mundane way. We walk to the office, we work in the office, we come home on the train, we say hello to our family and then we die.<br/>And then <i>
  <b>Erikson</b>
</i> comes in and reminds us that we have another whole world of passion, of love, of frustration, of sorrow, of tragedy, of desire. You know, t</span>
  <span id="freeText13216302451526824573" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Never mind the truth. The past is what I say it is. <br>That is the freedom of teaching the ignorant."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>You know, we spend our lives in ordinary mundane affairs. We behave in a mundane way, we dress in a mundane way. We walk to the office, we work in the office, we come home on the train, we say hello to our family and then we die.<br>And then <i>
  <b>Erikson</b>
</i> comes in and reminds us that we have another whole world of passion, of love, of frustration, of sorrow, of tragedy, of desire. You know, the entire range of human emotions available – through a book.<br><br>It is a remarkable window, this book. It provides a good time, or an adventure, or an escape. <br>Or even an excuse for us to be heroes, or a part-time villains <i>(because, let’s be frank, nobody wants to end up a villain forever after).</i> <br>It provides an access to someone else’s train of thoughts and within it a whole new point of view, of this imaginary world, or perhaps, even the real world that surrounds us.<br><br><i>
  <b>Reapers Gale</b>
</i> is a seventh book in <i>
  <b>The Malazan Book of the Fallen</b>
</i> series and twenty first on my chronological reading order which includes both <i>
  <b>Steven Erikson’s</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>Ian C. Esslemont’s</b>
</i> work.<br>The story in it follows one year after the events from previous two books, <i>
  <b>Midnight Tides</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>Bonehunters.</b>
</i> <br>We’re back on the continent of <i>
  <b>Lether</b>
</i> where we finally witness convergence of the characters and collision of their respective worlds, philosophies, powers, swords and – cussers. <br>Oh yes. <i>
  <b>Malazans</b>
</i> are here.<br><br>Empire of Lether is conquered by <i>
  <b>Tiste Edur.</b>
</i> On the throne sits <i>
  <b>Emperor of Thousand Deaths – Rhulad,</b>
</i> surrounded by Lether bureaucrats, which successfully isolated him from his fellow tribesmen, leaving him all alone with the whispers of previous betrayals, doubts and regrets. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518619207i/25059364._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Two opposing people now found themselves united, exploiting fallacies of each other’s systems of power and hierarchical structures: Edur got the crown – but does the crown wield real power?<br><br><i>
  <b>“The winners never won, because the losers refused to lose. An insane war.”</b>
</i><br><br>Tiste Edur struck, then Kingdom of Lether, pre-emptively, in response to the threat of losing their land and resources. A sort of economic war that, through fighting to avoid cultural assimilation and end of their independence, quite paradoxically grew into conquest of their own.<br>But, within a year of their occupation of Lether people, they have realized that a far more subtle conquest had taken place – conquest of which they were the losers.<br><br><i>
  <b>“They are here. On this shore. The Malazans are on our shore. And they burned their ships.”</b>
</i><br><br>Finally, on the distant, never before explored continent, Malazan professional soldiers get to do what they were made for. Away with the columns, away with the marches, belay with the orders of the high command and their chess wars. Now it’s the time for Guerilla warfare. And Malazans are bloody and vicious in it.<br><br>After seemingly losing their purpose, cursed in endless following bloody footsteps in the shadows of their predecessors, never to fulfill their expectations, <i>
  <b>Bonehunters</b>
</i> are lost. <br>There are big shoes to fill: <i>
  <b>Dassem Ultor,</b>
</i> first sword of Empire. The legendary <i>
  <b>Bridbeburners.</b>
</i> Worshiped <i>
  <b>Coltain’s 7th</b>
</i> army. Each name heavy with legends of their deeds, justified with their purpose.<br>Bonehunters were hurt. They are taking everything away from them. First battle. First win. Their own people doubted in legitimacy of their actions, they even tried to take the truth from them.<br>Well, <i>
  <b>Adjunct Tavore</b>
</i> of the house <i>
  <b>Paran,</b>
</i> will have none of that.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Compassion is never enough. Nor is the hunger for vengeance. <br>But, for now, for what awaits us, perhaps they will do. <br>We are the Bonehunters, and sail to another name. Beyond Aren, beyond Raraku and beyond Y’Ghatan, we now cross the world to find the first name that will be truly our own. Shared by none other. <br>We sail to give answer.”</b>
</i><br><br>While we wait for inevitable clash between the Empires, others are questing.<br><br>Tiste Edur <i>
  <b>Fear Sengar</b>
</i> and albino <i>
  <b>Tiste Andii Silchas Ruin</b>
</i> are on a quest of finding the soul of Edur’s deity <i>
  <b>Scara Bandaris, Scabandari Bloodeye,</b>
</i> but each with their own purpose. One to ask his God to help his hostage brother, the other, seemingly on quest for vengeance against that God, because in distant past, he was betrayed and stabbed in back by him.<br><br>Other quest involves another Tiste Edur, <i>
  <b>Trull Sengar,</b>
</i> a <i>
  <b>T’lan Imass Onrack T’emlava</b>
</i> and a wizard <i>
  <b>Ben Adaephon Delat,</b>
</i> who are send to find <i>‘the borders of a dreamworld.’</i> <br><br>Of course, as with every other of his books, we are introduced with a complete new cast of characters, tribes and nations. <br>This time those are united tribes of <i>
  <b>Awl</b>
</i> that rebel against oppressing Letheri Empire, led by <i>
  <b>Redmask,</b>
</i> a mortal sword of <i>
  <b>K’Chain Che’Malle.</b>
</i> Which, of course, means that at his side he has two beautiful beasts, <i>
  <b>K’El</b>
</i> hunters <i>
  <b>Sag’Churok</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>Gunth Mach.</b>
</i> <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518618985i/25059339._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>And combined, they are as vicious and deadly as they are beautiful.<br><br>And, of course, <i>
  <b>Karsa’s</b>
</i> there. Glorious in his character's mediocrity. <br>I know that there are a lot of fans of this character. To me, however, he brings this sense of boredom and predictability, something that I'm not used reading in these books.<br>But, I have complained about him and explained my reasons why I feel like that in depth in reviews for previous books, so I'm not going to do that again.<br><br>I guess that, after seven books in the series you highly enjoy reading, it's not that strange finding yourself at a loss of superlatives. Mainly because you don't want to sound repetitive. Saying again and again, how this is, in your honest opinion, the best high fantasy series - ever.<br>So, instead of repeating what's already established and exploring that in depth yet again, I mainly want to focus on problems and acknowledge that they exist in this book. <br><br>It takes a while for this book to start, sort to say. Although we begin with known characters, and while we are getting familiar with new setting and the surroundings, first time we actually feel like at home, is when Bonehunters enter the fray. <br>And the reason behind that, in my opinion, is because of what they bring.<br>Change of pacing, which until that point felt slow and repetitive, substantially gets better because of the structural narrative of how they were portrayed in this book.<br><br>Bonehunters, as a unit, are spread out all around the empire in minor units consisting of 15 soldiers.<br>Many of which get their own point of view. <br>And this, besides making pacing better, works on other levels as well, like getting familiar with the soldiers, which means that departure with them will be harder.<br>And I'll stop there.<br><br><i>
  <b>Sheltatha Lore, Sukul Ankhadu, Menandore rift.</b>
</i><br><i>(Going from three-dimensionality of a character to only one):</i><br><br>This is a problem that partially will have people who've read Kharkanas prequels.<br>Those of you who have read Kharkanas prequels already met these three sisters/cousins and explored some of those characters in depth, as well as members of their families.<br>Especially Sukul Ankhadu, who has a prominent role in those books, a character who is highly likable, and also, why not, both understandable and relatable. <br>So, it's much explored in depth characters that, in this book, you couldn't have possibly feel that.<br>Actually, if you remember what I have said here about Sukul Ankhadu while reading the book, you would probably think me mad.<br>That's because, sadly, she and her sisters/cousins are nothing but words on a paper. There's no depth whatsoever about these characters.<br><i>(But they veer into dragons and provide great battle sequences, so I guess, some of you are here for that...)</i><br><br>After <i>
  <b>Deadhouse Gates</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>Memories of Ice,</b>
</i> this is probably the toughest to get through emotionally.<br>Those of you who have read these two books I have mentioned, probably know that Deadhouse Gates is tough to go through mostly because of the themes that exploits, while Memories of Ice, on the other hand, is excruciatingly hard because of the characters and your emotional investment in them.<br>Reapers Gale combines both of that, just in a slightly lesser quantity.<br><br>In conclusion: brace yourselves. Each for different reasons.<br>Not an impeccable book, but highly enjoyable.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518618144i/25059273._SX540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>3.83/5</b>
</i><br><br><i>
  <b>Kharkanas Trilogy<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2167504768?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Forge of Darkness</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1462617190?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Fall of Light</a><br><br>Path to Ascendancy series<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1464500203?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dancer's Lament</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189195888?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Landing</a><br><br>Malazan Empire series<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1462615386?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Of Knives</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1462615415?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Return of the Crimson Guard</a><br><br>Malazan Book of the Fallen series<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2203966666?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Gardens of the Moon</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2215973985?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Gates</a><br><a Chains</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265295938?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a><br><br><a   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200411270" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1200411270?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1200411270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18038082340971676985">I apologise if this is not the most polished of reviews. I have to be honest, I am still speechless from what happened in the last quarter of this book.<br/><br/>To begin - most of my favourite characters from the books thus far were featured here. It brings two story arcs together. The relationship of the Edur/ Letherii in Letheras and the surrounding areas and also the Bone-hunters.<br/><br/>A lot of new characters are introduced (again! - how large can this cast get?* see the end of review). Some very memorable </span>
  <span id="freeText18038082340971676985" style="display:none">I apologise if this is not the most polished of reviews. I have to be honest, I am still speechless from what happened in the last quarter of this book.<br /><br />To begin - most of my favourite characters from the books thus far were featured here. It brings two story arcs together. The relationship of the Edur/ Letherii in Letheras and the surrounding areas and also the Bone-hunters.<br /><br />A lot of new characters are introduced (again! - how large can this cast get?* see the end of review). Some very memorable but none more so than dim-witted kind hearted super powerful mage Beak. <br /><br />The introduction of so many new faces did make it confusing during some of the battle scenes between the Letherii and Redmask's rebels. I kept having to revert back to the Dramatis Personae to remember who was on each side. The battle scenes were complex too. Very War &amp; Peace like. <br /><br />There are a lot of very fast POV segments throughout the book. Showing so many viewpoints we are really very lucky to analyse a work from so many wonderful, complex perspectives. <br /><br />I enjoyed following Silchas Ruin, Fear Sengar, Clip, Seren et al... knowing that this crew's journey to find Scabandari Bloodeye's soul was highly unpredictable and slightly nerve-wracking. Tehol &amp; Buggs banter is as hilarious as ever. It was also cool that Trull Sengar and Onrack meet up and cross paths with Quick Ben and Hedge. I do get the vibe that at the end of the Malazan Book of the Fallen - most the characters are going to know each other personally. Lol. <br /><br />The ending blew my mind. Some parts were just a bit too mean. &amp; People think the deaths in Game of Thrones come as a shock??! I had to re-read some of the scenes about seven times just to get my head around it to make sure I hadn't misanalysed the context. (I hadn't) So many touching moments when people realise their lovers or friends are dead. I need to recompose myself before I can allow myself back into this amazing, beautiful, heartless and grotesque world. <br /><br />*He probably added so many characters to replace the ones that are killed off :'(..... Peace.<br />James @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youandibooks.wordpress.com">www.youandibooks.wordpress.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18038082340971676985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_900630842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630842" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900630842?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11532022-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900630842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12794846132215380151">Well, this took me longer than any other book in the Malazan series. Possibly longer than any book I've read during the last few years. But I prevailed in the end.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen reviews:</i>
</b><br/>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271498' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gardens of the Moon</a><br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630799' rel='nofollow noopener'>Deadhouse Gates</a><br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630812' rel='nofollow noopener'>Memories of Ice</a><br/>#4 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630817' rel='nofollow noopener'>House of Chains</a><br/>#5 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630830' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midnight Tides</a><br/>#6 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630838' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bonehunters</a><br/>#7 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630842' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reaper's Gale</a><br/>#8 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630845' rel='nofollow noopener'>Toll the Hounds</a><br/>#9 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630849' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dust of Dreams</a><br/>#10 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630875' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crippled God</a></span>
  <span id="freeText12794846132215380151" style="display:none">Well, this took me longer than any other book in the Malazan series. Possibly longer than any book I've read during the last few years. But I prevailed in the end.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen reviews:</i>
</b><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271498" rel="nofollow noopener">Gardens of the Moon</a><br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630799" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Gates</a><br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630812" rel="nofollow noopener">Memories of Ice</a><br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630817" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Chains</a><br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630830" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a><br />#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630838" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a><br />#7 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630842" rel="nofollow noopener">Reaper's Gale</a><br />#8 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630845" rel="nofollow noopener">Toll the Hounds</a><br />#9 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630849" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust of Dreams</a><br />#10 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900630875" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crippled God</a></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51188905-michael-britt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877172250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2175816703979715037">I'm not crying, you're crying. <br/><br/>This has, by far, the saddest death scenes yet. The deaths themselves weren't that sad, but Erikson makes them heartbreaking. There's no way to really go into more depth without huge spoilers. <br/><br/>As far as the story goes, Erikson hits it out of the park, yet again. Our cast is most of the people we've already met: we have some Malazans, the Bonehunters, Letherii (which I hate with a passion, save Tehol) and the Edur. We also get to meet Silchas Ruin, Anomander Rake's </span>
  <span id="freeText2175816703979715037" style="display:none">I'm not crying, you're crying. <br /><br />This has, by far, the saddest death scenes yet. The deaths themselves weren't that sad, but Erikson makes them heartbreaking. There's no way to really go into more depth without huge spoilers. <br /><br />As far as the story goes, Erikson hits it out of the park, yet again. Our cast is most of the people we've already met: we have some Malazans, the Bonehunters, Letherii (which I hate with a passion, save Tehol) and the Edur. We also get to meet Silchas Ruin, Anomander Rake's brother. Who we're told is the coldest of the brothers, which is scary to think of. <br /><br />The battle scenes, especially the one between just 2 people,at the end, gave me goosebumps. It shows just how scary one particular warrior really is in battle. <br /><br />These reviews will be getting shorter and shorter due to just about anything I could say would be a major spoiler.</span>

<div id="review_1622085196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622085196" />
    <a title="Scott  Hitchcock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50894754-scott-hitchcock"><img alt="Scott  Hitchcock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459187975p2/50894754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622085196?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott  Hitchcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott  Hitchcock" href="/user/show/50894754-scott-hitchcock">Scott  Hitchcock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8623112-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=grimdark">grimdark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622085196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13105083679544047363">Upon Reread this book read as it did the first time. The first third is a lot of the Awl, the Patriotists and the Liberty Consign. It's sends a lot of important political messages with direct parallels to American history but I was again glad when it was over and at the end of book two Yan Tovis utters music to every readers ears <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[They are here. On this shore. The Malazans are on our shore.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>Tehol and Bugg do what Tehol and Bugg do and amuse us with banter ranging fr</span>
  <span id="freeText13105083679544047363" style="display:none">Upon Reread this book read as it did the first time. The first third is a lot of the Awl, the Patriotists and the Liberty Consign. It's sends a lot of important political messages with direct parallels to American history but I was again glad when it was over and at the end of book two Yan Tovis utters music to every readers ears <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are here. On this shore. The Malazans are on our shore.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Tehol and Bugg do what Tehol and Bugg do and amuse us with banter ranging from absurd to clever but ever mixed with a political overtone. <br /><br />This book majorly belongs to the marines. If you didn't love them leaving Y'Ghatan, besides WTF is wrong with you, you have to love them in this tale. All their backstories, their banter and bickering, concern and empathy. <br /><br />But it also lives up to its nickname Weaper's Gale. Just as gut-wrenching the second time. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Beak, Toc, Trull......and then the survivors Tool, Onrack, Seren.....so much pain and anguish.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Then in the end SE does what SE does and produces yet another massive convergerance with multiple plot lines all crashing together in truly epic fashion. Simply Brilliant. <br /><br />I think I caught more that I missed in this reread than any of the others. So many little symbolic details. Some setup long ago and some still far reaching. This series makes all other "epic" series look like novellas. <br /><br />-------- Original review<br /><br />So you’ve finished the 6th installment the Bonehunters and you’re thinking here we go a clash of worlds. Malazan vs Letherii, Rhulad vs Karsa vs Icarium steel cage death match, Quick Ben vs Shadowthorne……..NOPE. Dear reader did you actually think we would pick up anywhere else but in the midst of a hundred new characters and storylines? Foolish mortals. <br /><br />The start was like the first book of House of Chains or the start of Midnight Tides. Thankfully a lot of characters like Karsa, Silchas Ruin and others started to cycle in but I was never so happy to read:“They are here. On this shore. The Malazans are on our shore.”<br /><br />I loved all the Malazan parts. I loved the story line of Ruin, Fear, Seren, Udinaas and Kettle. I loved the story arc of Quick, Hedge, Trull and Onrack. The quick screen time of Karsa, Icarium, Shadownthrone, Menendore and others also great. I found the Letherii parts slow and tough at times. Even Bug and Tehol’s humor seemed a little trite compared to the camaraderie of the Malazans and other groups. <br /><br />Chapter 22 has to go down as one of the top ten of the series and perhaps the most heart wrenching of them all which is saying something considering events in Deadhouse and Memories. Chapter 23 also very sad and a scene three dragons and a wizard that I would love to see on the big screen. <br />Starvald Demelain, the warren of dragons……………did not see that coming. <br /><br />The ending had a lot of surprises. Some good, some bad and a lot more sadness. <br /><br />All in all just another amazing chapter in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13105083679544047363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10309807522039315622">4.5 Stars. <br/><br/>This one is incredibly hard to rate. The middle 1/3 or so dragged as much as any Malazan book (and these books <i> drag </i> in places) since book 1.While some of the plot threads were still interesting, if somewhat slow-paced (the Malazan soldier's) some were pretty much dead in the water with seemingly nothing happening but a load of depressing philosphising (The quest to find Scabandari Blood-eye). However the final quarter brought pretty much every previously dull and stagnant plot-threa</span>
  <span id="freeText10309807522039315622" style="display:none">4.5 Stars. <br /><br />This one is incredibly hard to rate. The middle 1/3 or so dragged as much as any Malazan book (and these books <i> drag </i> in places) since book 1.While some of the plot threads were still interesting, if somewhat slow-paced (the Malazan soldier's) some were pretty much dead in the water with seemingly nothing happening but a load of depressing philosphising (The quest to find Scabandari Blood-eye). However the final quarter brought pretty much every previously dull and stagnant plot-thread to life, ramped the pace up to 11 and delivered one of my favourite endings, in a series chocked full of awesome endings (I especially appreciated that this ending didn't feel like Erikson was trying to force as much epicness as possible into it like some other ones, this one felt like a much more natural progression from the rest of the story). <br /><br />Full review to come.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687181179" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12539891594865464352">I now understand why fans call it Weeper's Gale.<br/><br/>Like MT, the Letherii storyline took me longer to get into than some of the other Malazan books. In RG, Erikson has undertaken more storylines with more characters while at the same time trying to close off some stories. I wasn't sure he could bring it all together at the end, but by now, I should expect nothing but greatness from him.<br/><br/>I would have to say that my favourite storylines in RG were the ones that got the least amount of pages. I didn't d</span>
  <span id="freeText12539891594865464352" style="display:none">I now understand why fans call it Weeper's Gale.<br /><br />Like MT, the Letherii storyline took me longer to get into than some of the other Malazan books. In RG, Erikson has undertaken more storylines with more characters while at the same time trying to close off some stories. I wasn't sure he could bring it all together at the end, but by now, I should expect nothing but greatness from him.<br /><br />I would have to say that my favourite storylines in RG were the ones that got the least amount of pages. I didn't dislike the others, but I found myself being drawn to characters I already knew. Karsa and Icarium's POVs are the most memorable in my mind, but all of the Malazan characters were a welcome addition to the novel after book one. A couple of my favourite stories: Tehol and Bugg, Toc, Samar Dev, Icarium, Karsa, Silchas Ruin, Quick Ben.<br /><br />Chapter 22 was legendary. It was one of the best chapters in the whole series and I'm still in shock, but it seems <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Toc will still have a role even though he died, so there is some good news for my favourite one-eyed character <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. This chapter, and the last book of the novel in general, was flipped between POVs so perfectly; I really didn't want to put the book down at that point.</span>

  <span id="freeText1019507736966815025" style="display:none">I don't feel like writing a review so this is gonna be a mini rant with a spoiler included.<br /><br />This is, for me, the weakest book in the series so far.
