<div id="review_318362909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318362909" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318362909?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8623112-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318362909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12926846240029696425"><b>
  <u>Initial Read</u>
</b><br/><br/>Another solid entry in the Malazan Series. In this 7th book we have a convergence of story arcs started in "Midnight Tides" as well as "The Bonehunters" and throw in a couple more that nobody really cares about and adds a couple hundred unnecessary pages and you have another epic adventure with its unique brand that is The Malazan Series.<br/><br/>So here we have the rebel Bonehunters having escaped from Malaz appointing themselves as the avengers of the Edur/Letherii atrocities committed </span>
  <span id="freeText12926846240029696425" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Initial Read</u>
</b><br /><br />Another solid entry in the Malazan Series. In this 7th book we have a convergence of story arcs started in "Midnight Tides" as well as "The Bonehunters" and throw in a couple more that nobody really cares about and adds a couple hundred unnecessary pages and you have another epic adventure with its unique brand that is The Malazan Series.<br /><br />So here we have the rebel Bonehunters having escaped from Malaz appointing themselves as the avengers of the Edur/Letherii atrocities committed on the Malazan Empire.<br />Yes, that means we get to see two of my favourites Tehol and Bugg as they plan to bring down the financial machinery of the Letherii empire with the humour and wise cracks(and pet chickens?)flying left right and centre.<br />We have the badass marines/Bonehunters ie Fiddler, Hellian, and co, slicing, smashing, blasting, drinking and rooting their way across Lether as they head for the capital.<br />We have Quick Ben, we have dragon battles, mage battles, sword and exploding crossbow battles.<br />We have Sichas ruin and Kettle and if you thought you knew what the deal was with those two and the Azath house in the previous book - you dont (unless you cheat and read the wikis) You'll never guess where that convoluted story arc ends up.<br />We have Trull Sengar and Onrack.<br /><br />In other words we have too many characters, too may story arcs, but in all that we are well rewarded in the end. I even shed a tear. Yes, Steve Erikson might have taken 7 books to do it, but he finally managed to make me care enough about SOME of the characters - enough so to piss me off when he kills one in particular - Congratulation you a - - hole!<br /><br />Loved the book - deducted one star for the extra 200 to 300 pages of unnecessary meaningless story arcs that went nowhere and add nothing. But thats Malazan for you. <br /><br />7 down, 3 books to go.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Reread</u>
</b><br /><br />On my second read through I don't have a lot to add from the initial review. It was, again, a superior reading experience on the reread and I am more attached to more of the characters this time round. However, I still feel there was a bit of bloat with the Awl story arc, which is why I'm keeping my rating at...<br /><br /><br />4 stars <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12926846240029696425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857542104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16888503219456544582"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>For me, this is the first of the series that starts to close the circle. There are endings within these pages that are devastating, some that bring a tearful smile, and some that bring a joyful 'yeah, you got yours'... Of course, being Erikson, that doesn't mean there aren't new characters and new questions; he has a deep and abiding dislike of simplicity. Save a few spellbinding moments, it's not a book that is in the running for the top spot, but it serves well to signal the beginning</span>
  <span id="freeText16888503219456544582" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />For me, this is the first of the series that starts to close the circle. There are endings within these pages that are devastating, some that bring a tearful smile, and some that bring a joyful 'yeah, you got yours'... Of course, being Erikson, that doesn't mean there aren't new characters and new questions; he has a deep and abiding dislike of simplicity. Save a few spellbinding moments, it's not a book that is in the running for the top spot, but it serves well to signal the beginning of the end.</span>

It doesn't get more epic than this. </span>

I'm not saying anything remotely new here but these books keep getting better. It's just a tremendously entertaining series that doesn't insult my grey matter and rewards the effort required to read. </span>

<div id="review_494546219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/494546219" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494546219?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553813166" href="/book/show/2893217-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=malazan-fallen">malazan-fallen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494546219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer488010988863986777"><b>Executive Summary:</b> After what has to be my favorite of the series <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/478951.The_Bonehunters__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___6_' title='The Bonehunters (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #6) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bonehunters</a>, this one is a big letdown. Too many new characters really bog the story down for far too long, but it ends strong enough to save it from being a bad book.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>This book seems to take everything about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_' title='Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midnight Tides</a> and ramp it up. Unlike that book however, I didn't find myself confused and frustrated at the beginning. I was simply uninterested. So unlike Midnight Tides where I enjoyed the story once I go</span>
  <span id="freeText488010988863986777" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> After what has to be my favorite of the series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/478951.The_Bonehunters__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___6_" title="The Bonehunters (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #6) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a>, this one is a big letdown. Too many new characters really bog the story down for far too long, but it ends strong enough to save it from being a bad book.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />This book seems to take everything about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_" title="Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a> and ramp it up. Unlike that book however, I didn't find myself confused and frustrated at the beginning. I was simply uninterested. So unlike Midnight Tides where I enjoyed the story once I got my bearings, this one just kept leaving me bored for far too much of the book.<br /><br />One of the flaws I often see in Epic fantasy is introducing too many characters and subplots that it bogs the story down. This is the main fault I found with the Wheel of Time series that could badly use editing to make books 8-10 into 1 or 2 much tighter novels.<br /><br />This one isn't quite at that extreme, but I hope that things turn around with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/938544.Toll_the_Hounds__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___8_" title="Toll the Hounds (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #8) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Toll the Hounds</a>.<br /><br />The Letherii/Tiste Edur story just isn't that interesting to me. Maybe it's because I find almost no likable characters in the bunch apart from Tehol and Bugg. All of the new characters, especially the Patriotists are despicable. <br /><br />That's all well and good, but I feel Mr. Erikson spends entirely too much time convincing just how despicable they are. I think there were enough (or nearly enough) characters from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_" title="Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a> that could have been used to tell this story without adding so many new faces.<br /><br />Thankfully the Malazans come to the rescue of this story, albeit a lot later than I would have liked. Old favorites like Fiddler and Quick Ben and the banter of the Marines are a relief from the tedium that is the Letherii/Edur story.<br /><br />Mr. Erikson seems to always write really terrible beginnings (even though I know he's capable of writing good ones) but really excellent endings. This one is no different. However I won't let another strong ending fool me into forgetting about how bored I was for far too much of this novel.<br /><br />There were enough enjoyable chapters in this book to save it from a 2-star rating, but overall this has been the weakest novel in the series for me so far. Readers who enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_" title="Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a> more than I did may come away with a different opinion, but I for one am happy to move on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="488010988863986777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1902566062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902566062" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613919-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483904179p2/2613919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1902566062?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/2613919-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1902566062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer648697869163134506">5 Stars <br/><br/><br/>Reaper's Gale by Steven Erikson is the seventh book in The Malazan Book of the Fallen series and it is a lot...more. This is the best and worst book in the series so far! Reaper's Gale would be a pinnacle of the epic fantasy genre if it underwent at least some editing. Being book number seven, I knew and expected to have far too many characters and points of view to really know what was going on. I made a mistake in deciding that I was going to dive into this monster and attempt to read </span>
  <span id="freeText648697869163134506" style="display:none">5 Stars <br /><br /><br />Reaper's Gale by Steven Erikson is the seventh book in The Malazan Book of the Fallen series and it is a lot...more. This is the best and worst book in the series so far! Reaper's Gale would be a pinnacle of the epic fantasy genre if it underwent at least some editing. Being book number seven, I knew and expected to have far too many characters and points of view to really know what was going on. I made a mistake in deciding that I was going to dive into this monster and attempt to read it over a couple of days. I should have been patient. There are more than 25 points of view and three to four times that number in characters to keep track of. It took a herculean effort to not give up to the difficulties. <br /><br />Deciding to binge read this book made it much harder than it had to be. Of course there are far too many characters and views, but if taken in the right way, no fan would ever care as every word in this enormous novel comes across as perfect. Erikson has a pedestal all too himself as other writers can only attempt to reach his greatness. He is the master. The final quarter of this novel(two more regular books in length) are non stop action, emotion, jaw dropping, cheering out loud, breathtaking, heart pumping, fist beating, and curse dropping. You may never experience anything like it again. Freaking awesome, I mean really freaking incredible as is wow wtf did I just read and experience.<br /><br />Holy shit I devoured it. I lived it. I absolutely loved it! Steven Erikson, you are freaking cool.<br /><br /><br /><br />A few cool snippets from this unbelievable read... <br /><br /><br /><br />"—and Quick Ben, who was running towards the roof's edge, his hands raised and sorcery building round him as if he was the prow of a ship cutting through water."<br /><br /><br /><br />......<br /><br /><br /><br />"'The Azath.' 'Very good. You always were sharp, Ben Delat.' A grunt. 'I've not used that version of my name in a long time.' 'Oh? When was the last time –do you recall?' 'These Azath,' Quick Ben said, clearly ignoring the question. 'The House of Shadow itself, here in this realm, correct? Somehow, it has usurped the gate, the original gate. Kurald Emurlahn. The House exists both as a cast shadow and as its true physical manifestation. No distinction can be made between the two. A nexus . . . but that is not unusual for Azath constructs, is it? What is, however, is that the gate to Kurald Emurlahn was vulnerable in the first place, to such a usurpation.' 'Necessity, I expect,' said Cotillion, frowning at seeing a slow sweep of broad ripples approach the shore, their source somewhere further out. Not at all what it seems . . ."<br /><br /><br />.......<br /><br /><br />"She had chosen to remain as she was, rather than veer into her Soletaken form. That would come later. And so she walked across the plain, through the high grasses of the basin. On a ridge directly ahead stood two figures. One was a ghost, but maybe something more than just a ghost. The other was a mage, and without question more than just a mage."<br /><br /><br /><br />......<br /><br /><br />The Malazan Book of the Fallen series is simply the very best of the fantasy genre and deserving equal praise for it's literary prowess.<br /><br />If you haven't read these... Well, remedy it.<br /><br /><br />A week after finishing this book, I can't stop thinking about it. A couple more notes. This book is really all about the "B's"...<br /><br />Beak, Ben, Bottle, and Bugg steal the show.<br /><br />This book is not for those that dislike the unreliable narrator as this book is about a place where things are not always what they appear to be.<br /><br />The action is simply unbelievable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="648697869163134506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=lgbtqa">lgbtqa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744947734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7770685556707010825">When I first started <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/459064.Reaper_s_Gale__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___7_' title='Reaper's Gale (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #7) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reaper's Gale</a>, I was apprehensive. I knew a few people who said it wasn't that good compared with the rest of the series and they really struggled with it. I knew it picked up from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_' title='Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midnight Tides</a>, my least favorite of the series so far. I ended up loving <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/459064.Reaper_s_Gale__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___7_' title='Reaper's Gale (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #7) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reaper's Gale</a>. Perhaps part of that is understanding how things work on Lether, being familiar with the characters, and how the storylines begin to converge with characters from Seven Cities.<br/><br/>This book weaves together storyli</span>
  <span id="freeText7770685556707010825" style="display:none">When I first started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/459064.Reaper_s_Gale__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___7_" title="Reaper's Gale (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #7) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Reaper's Gale</a>, I was apprehensive. I knew a few people who said it wasn't that good compared with the rest of the series and they really struggled with it. I knew it picked up from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_" title="Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a>, my least favorite of the series so far. I ended up loving <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/459064.Reaper_s_Gale__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___7_" title="Reaper's Gale (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #7) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Reaper's Gale</a>. Perhaps part of that is understanding how things work on Lether, being familiar with the characters, and how the storylines begin to converge with characters from Seven Cities.<br /><br />This book weaves together storylines from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_" title="Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/478951.The_Bonehunters__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___6_" title="The Bonehunters (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #6) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a>. We have the continuing story of Tehol and Bugg and their efforts to bring down the Letherii economy, Rhulad's progressive madness, Seren Pedac and company's journey, woven in with the arrival of the Tiste Edur fleet bringing champions to combat Rhulad (Karsa and Icarium!), and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The Adjunct's army arriving on Lether <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />There's quite a few new characters introduced early on. With the end of the series drawing nigh, most authors would start to wrap some things up and wouldn't bring in a whole cast of new people. Not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/31232.Steven_Erikson" title="Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Steven Erikson</a>. He never takes it easy on the reader which is why I've grown to love him so much. I didn't have strong feelings about most of the new characters but that doesn't bother me because I love being in the Malazan world so much and they made it a deeper experience.<br /><br />There are a few parts of the book I didn't like or understand what their purpose was. The whole Awl storyline seems to exist purely to bring back an old friend. As happy as I was to catch up with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Toc the Younger <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I think this could have been done in a better way. The battles between the Awl and Letherii bored me, along with the Shake. I wasn't into the Patriotists storyline either but ended up enjoying it by the end.<br /><br />I loved this book because we got to spend time with old favorites such as Onrack, Trull, Tehol, Bugg, Karsa, and Quick Ben but also because it made me really feel for not only the older characters but some new ones as well, particularly Beak. His story was really moving and nearly brought me to tears.<br /><br />Speaking of tears, one character's death did make me cry. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Trull was stabbed in the heart, I felt like I got stabbed, too. It was shocking, cruel, and incredibly heartbreaking. Trull was one of my favorite characters. I loved the time he spend with Onrack and they developed such a beautiful friendship. His death didn't feel like it was gratuitous either. Erikson didn't kill him just to shock his readers (GRRM, I am looking at you). I have yet to recover and I don't think I ever will. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />One issue I have had with the series so far is the romance. Most of the pairings never felt natural and never elicited any emotional response from me. This is the first book where the romance is clicking for me, particularly <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Karsa and Samar Dev <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm rooting for those two to get together. <br /><br />I'll wrap it up since this is getting long. Bottom line: I loved this book despite its flaws.<br /><br /><b>A</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7770685556707010825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119165893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119165893" />
    <a title="Jonathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272061-jonathan"><img alt="Jonathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243372852p2/272061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119165893?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan" href="/user/show/272061-jonathan">Jonathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553813166" href="/book/show/2893217-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119165893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8066848739436230987">I can see that the overarching story might add up to a wonderful jigsaw, but Erikson is a demented pounder of the keyboard, someone needs to edit him savagely, take away his computer and make him write longhand. He has long since lost control of his creation. As Stalin may have said 'Quantity has a Quality all of its own', it pounds your mind into numbed submission as you trudge towards the slopes of Mount Doom, bearing the ring of steadily reducing expectations.<br/><br/>After 500 pages of this the 7th M</span>
  <span id="freeText8066848739436230987" style="display:none">I can see that the overarching story might add up to a wonderful jigsaw, but Erikson is a demented pounder of the keyboard, someone needs to edit him savagely, take away his computer and make him write longhand. He has long since lost control of his creation. As Stalin may have said 'Quantity has a Quality all of its own', it pounds your mind into numbed submission as you trudge towards the slopes of Mount Doom, bearing the ring of steadily reducing expectations.<br /><br />After 500 pages of this the 7th Malazan book of the fallen, the Malazan arrive. There are still 700 pages to go, but at least the story picks up a bit. Erikson is a master of repetition and meandering conversations. Yes we get it, the Letherii Empire has been conquered but its conqueror's have no control. We really don't care after the fifth time someone says this. Likewise the number of very similar skirmishes and pointless rapes do nothing for me.<br /><br />Erikson does the worst resolutions to conflicts one can imagine, after say 3 or 400 pages of build up you expect something special, but what you get is a couple of pages, of 'oh he got killed'.<br /><br />The Malazan wander around with high explosives, but 'fight' ever so bravely against the poor saps armed only with swords. I can't ever believe in magic that can't remotely detonate gunpowder, you need only read Grunts by Mary gentle to see how pitifully high technology performs in such an environment.<br /><br />Let us hope that Erikson finishes this soon, or is otherwise forced to write something new, short and focused. This rambling sprawl has good elements drowned in padding and power inflation, virtually anyone could do anything, there is no sense of certain characters being special.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8066848739436230987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1118024714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1118024714" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Twerking To Beethoven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Twerking To Beethoven" href="/user/show/8940772-twerking-to-beethoven">Twerking To Beethoven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553813166" href="/book/show/2893217-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8940772-twerking-to-beethoven?shelf=new-wave-of-canadian-heavy-metal">new-wave-of-canadian-heavy-metal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1118024714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15430913581509047086">With every installment of this series, I become more and more impressed. <br/><br/>Erikson writes epic fantasy on a level all his own. The world is massive and engaging. It is at once believable and yet otherworldly, creating a fusion of worlds that leaves your jaw hanging. I am amazed at how well he writes the characters and holds such a complex and huge story together, with each book at least 900-1000 pages.<br/><br/>In "Reaper's Gale" we finally see the two worlds, the Malazan and the Letherii, finally begin to </span>
  <span id="freeText15430913581509047086" style="display:none">With every installment of this series, I become more and more impressed. <br /><br />Erikson writes epic fantasy on a level all his own. The world is massive and engaging. It is at once believable and yet otherworldly, creating a fusion of worlds that leaves your jaw hanging. I am amazed at how well he writes the characters and holds such a complex and huge story together, with each book at least 900-1000 pages.<br /><br />In "Reaper's Gale" we finally see the two worlds, the Malazan and the Letherii, finally begin to converge. We get to see the Bonehunters as well as the Tiste Edur. But it wouldn't be Erikson if some new aspect were not introduced to add such colour and flavor to an already mind numbingly full bodied book. We see the Awl, the Benetract, an Ascendent previously undisclosed and a bunch of Elder gods.<br /><br />I could go on and on but I wouldn't do the book or Erikson justice. His writing is amazing. His world is amazing. Everything is amazing about this series. I think he is by far one of the best fantasy writers out there right now, and is one of the few authors who can write more than a three book series and make every single one of them an amazingly complex book that is also a page turner.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_416454862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416454862" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416454862?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416454862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16286055866874784647">The book returns to events in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_' title='Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midnight Tides</a>, namely conquest of Lethery Empire by Tiste Edur. Nobody (including the conquerors) is particularly happy about the results. On the top of this are the Bonehunters led by Adjunct Tavore with the mission of toppling of the current Empire. The combination of all of these leads to (supposedly) explosive conclusion. <br/><br/>This is probably the first book where I am still not sure about the rating. It is somewhere between 3 and 4 stars, so let us say 3.5 with 0.5</span>
  <span id="freeText16286055866874784647" style="display:none">The book returns to events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_" title="Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a>, namely conquest of Lethery Empire by Tiste Edur. Nobody (including the conquerors) is particularly happy about the results. On the top of this are the Bonehunters led by Adjunct Tavore with the mission of toppling of the current Empire. The combination of all of these leads to (supposedly) explosive conclusion. <br /><br />This is probably the first book where I am still not sure about the rating. It is somewhere between 3 and 4 stars, so let us say 3.5 with 0.5 stars for my respect for the series.<br /><br /><b>The Good</b><br />The results of the conquest I mentioned above are very... interesting and unexpected. Some of the really major high players are permanently out of the game, making it easier to keep track of the rest. There was a moment where Quick Ben finally appeared to be a total bad-ass. <br /><br /><b>The Ugly</b><br />The author spends half of the book introducing a lot of new characters with POV. We are talking about 7th book in the series, is it a little too late for this? I mean, there are a lot of them, like one new character per page. On the related note, POVs are switched way too often. <br /><br />It is very clear from the beginning how the book will end, but I have an impression the author did everything he could think of to postpone the ending; heck he even made Quick Ben look boring except for the moment I mentioned above. <br /><br />There is no explosive ending. Sure, some people die, but still this is the quietest ending of the series so far. <br /><br />So in conclusion, half of the book is worth 3 stars with another half being 4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16286055866874784647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170157846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170157846" />
    <a title="Traci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5024825-traci"><img alt="Traci" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356372450p2/5024825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170157846?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Traci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Traci" href="/user/show/5024825-traci">Traci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765348845" href="/book/show/5878388-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5024825-traci?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5024825-traci?shelf=aficionado-top-100-challenge">aficionado-top-100-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170157846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15149663361807563667">Done. Finally. This one took me awhile. I learned a few things with this book. Number one, I didn't have the stamina for a marathon Malazan reading. I think I sprained something in my brain in the attempt. I also learned that while Steven Erikson is a master of writing tragedy I don't care for his over the top humor. With a few exceptions, I do love Tehol and Bugg. And that hidden beneath this dark tale hides the heart of a romantic. And an author who can write male friendships like no one else </span>
  <span id="freeText15149663361807563667" style="display:none">Done. Finally. This one took me awhile. I learned a few things with this book. Number one, I didn't have the stamina for a marathon Malazan reading. I think I sprained something in my brain in the attempt. I also learned that while Steven Erikson is a master of writing tragedy I don't care for his over the top humor. With a few exceptions, I do love Tehol and Bugg. And that hidden beneath this dark tale hides the heart of a romantic. And an author who can write male friendships like no one else I have ever read.<br /><br />I spent the first half of this book in frustrating confusion. Too many characters. Too many plot points to keep track of. I stopped reading a few times. The only thing that kept me going was my love for the previous books and my nearness to the end of the series. <br /><br />And then somewhere I couldn't put it down. I spent the second half in dreadful anticipation of what was going to happen from page to page. So much tragedy in one book. No one character is "safe". And that knowledge makes for a nail biting read.<br /><br />Some high points for me were Beak, Toc the younger, and Trull story lines. I also liked getting back to the characters from Midnight Tides. <br /><br />I couldn't decide between a four or five star rating. The last half was an easy five for me. But I struggled in the first half. So a very high four. Days after reading this the end is still haunting my thoughts. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Just when Trull was becoming my favorite character.... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /> Can't wait to see where this series is going next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15149663361807563667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy" href="/user/show/37399719-tammy">Tammy</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765348845" href="/book/show/5878388-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1514514290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8066225862581037080">We're back to Lether.<br/>Reaper's Gale had sooo much going on, with arguably the most plot lines in a single book so far, it would have been a disaster if Erikson couldn't weave all these back together and deliver a convincing end. BUT HE DID, making this one of the best books i've ever read plot wise.<br/>I also believe this is the darkest book so far, I mean some nasty, gritty sh*t goes down here.<br/>STILL, it was able to produce so many emotional moments, giving you a nostalgic taste of what you felt in b</span>
  <span id="freeText8066225862581037080" style="display:none">We're back to Lether.<br />Reaper's Gale had sooo much going on, with arguably the most plot lines in a single book so far, it would have been a disaster if Erikson couldn't weave all these back together and deliver a convincing end. BUT HE DID, making this one of the best books i've ever read plot wise.<br />I also believe this is the darkest book so far, I mean some nasty, gritty sh*t goes down here.<br />STILL, it was able to produce so many emotional moments, giving you a nostalgic taste of what you felt in book 2 and 3. If an author can make you fight back tears, he's an artist Isn't he?<br /><br />My Stand out characters: Tehol (the Only) and Bugg, Trull Sengar and Onrack the Broken, Samar Dev, Toc Anaster, Fiddler, Beak, Bruthen Trana. Icarium Lifestealer. Silchas Ruin the Cruelest. Ben Adaephon Delat. <br />Karsa (look up badass in the dictionary I swear you'll see this guy with a grin, and a huge flint sword, staring back at you).<br />Again, never forget Hellian, Queen of taverns.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1263335094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263335094" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263335094?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8623112-reaper-s-gale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=epics">epics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263335094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1102321942843210711">With Reaper's Gale we have the convergence of the plot lines from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1202428310?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midnight Tides</a> (probably my favorite one so far) and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228336497?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bonehunters</a>. As I stated in my Bonehunters review, I thought it was mostly a book about getting pieces into a place, and boy did those movements pay off. We get a clash of the now Edur dominated (or is it!?!?!?!) Letherii Empire and the rag tag army of the Bonehunters. On top of that we still have Tehol Benedict and his loyal manservant Bugg running about committing a brilli</span>
  <span id="freeText1102321942843210711" style="display:none">With Reaper's Gale we have the convergence of the plot lines from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1202428310?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a> (probably my favorite one so far) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228336497?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bonehunters</a>. As I stated in my Bonehunters review, I thought it was mostly a book about getting pieces into a place, and boy did those movements pay off. We get a clash of the now Edur dominated (or is it!?!?!?!) Letherii Empire and the rag tag army of the Bonehunters. On top of that we still have Tehol Benedict and his loyal manservant Bugg running about committing a brilliant bit of economic sabotage, and Karsa and Icarium waiting around to duel the Emperor of a Thousand Deaths. Not to mention agitation and trouble on the Empire's borders. And I am leaving out a whole bunch of other fascinating plot lines with Quick Ben, the T'Lan Imass, Sichas Ruin, and a boat load more. As much as Erikson setting up pieces in the last book, he does a great job quickly putting them into play. This book was a non-stop roller-coaster through a whole bunch of different POVs.<br /><br /> One of the themes of this book was the end of things in the face of eternal certainty: ideas, people, ways of life.<blockquote>
  <i>Things end. Species die out. Faith in anything else was a conceit, the product of unchained ego, the curse of supreme self-importance.</i>
</blockquote> The two biggest entities this applies to are the Empire of Lether, who was recently conquered (but not really) by the Edur and the Awl, a nomadic people being displaced by Letherii business interests. In the case of the Empire, the reports of its conquests have been greatly exaggerated.<blockquote>
  <i>The Edur became the crown, settling easy upon the bloated gluttony of Lether, but does a crown possess will? Does the wearer buckle beneath its burden?</i>
</blockquote>You can take the Lether off the throne, but not the throne off Lether. The Edur.<blockquote>
  <i>The skein that held Lether together was resilient and far stronger than it appeared. What disturbed him the most was the ease with which that skein entwined all who found themselves in its midst.</i>
</blockquote>And the Edur have been somewhat subsumed by that seductive siren call. In total they were but a small portion of the Empire's population so they had to lean on existing human institutions to sure up their rule. As the The Who sang, <i>Meet the new boss, same as the old boss</i>.<br /><br />The Awl, on the other hand, are a broken people whose ageless way of life is threatened by the "progress" of Lether. Their tribes kept divided and weak, their leaders bought off, the spirit of the people despondent. Their very culture, which has persisted for thousands of years, is at risk of destruction. Out of the trackless plains comes Red Mask, an exiled Awl warrior who would reforge his people, change them and their way of life, to meet and repel the Letherii threat.<blockquote>
  <i>"This new way of fighting, War Leader, I see little honour in it."<br />"You speak true. There is none to be found. Such is necessity."<br />"Must necessity be surrender?"<br />"When the ways surrendered hold naught but the promise of failure, then yes. It must be done. They must be cast away.</i>
</blockquote> Oh, and he has two ancient, long thought extinct, lizard like creatures (with giant sword hands) whose raw strength is only matched by the mystery of their association with him.<br /><br />Erikson also takes this opportunity to expand upon the nexus of power and greed in societies.<blockquote>
  <i>Power shapes the face of the world. In itself, it is neither benign nor malicious, it is simply the tool by which its wielder reshapes all that is around him or herself, reshape it to suit his or her own... comforts. Of course, to express power is to enact tyranny, which can be most subtle and soft, or cruel and hard. Implicit in power is the threat of coercion.</i>
</blockquote> Unsurprisingly, power in Lether takes the form of cruel and hard. I mean, what is a totalitarian regime without a secret police force to strengthen its grip on society. And yes, they attract just the sort of person you would expect.<blockquote>
  <i>He wasn't much interested in beating his women, just in seeing them beaten. He understood his desire was perversion, but this organization - the Patriotists - was the perfect haven for people like him. Power and immunity, a most deadly combination.</i>
</blockquote>Of course it doesn't help that they are headed by an intelligent, if ruthless, operator whose understanding of human nature makes his truly terrifying.<blockquote>
  <i>A citizen with certainty can be swayed, turned, can be made into a most diligent ally. All one needs to do is find what threatens them the most. Ignite their fear, burn to cinders the foundations of their certainty, then offer an equally certain alternative way of thinking, of seeing the world. They will reach across, no matter how wide the gulf, and grasp and hold on to you with all their strength. No, the certain are not our enemies… our greatest enemies are those without certainty. Those with questions, the ones who regard our tidy answers with unquenchable skepticism.</i>
</blockquote>When thugs are in power, educated people were the first to feel their fists.<br /><br />What I liked about Erikson's conception of the Letherii Empire is how subtle the oppression it is. There are not massive slave markets (but there are masses of people who are slaves in all but name). There is not pervasive oppression (but plenty of oppression is doled out in the back alley). On the surface everything seems to be a capitalist paradise, where people can rise and fall on merit, but the structure of the society and economy is such that there are a few people at the very top while the vast majority toil in debt or in fear of becoming indebted.<blockquote>
  <i>Is there a difference between spilled blood and blood squeezed out slowly, excruciatingly, over the course of a foreshortened lifetime of stress, misery, anguish and despair - all in the name of some amorphous god that no-one dares call holy? Even as they bend knee and repeat the litany of sacred duty."</i>
</blockquote>So basically Lether is collapsing into a totalitarian state run in equal parts fanatics and the business elite with Edur as figure heads at the top. Into this volatile mix are thrown the Bonehunters, an exiled Malazan army seeking to revenge the atrocities committed against Malazan protectorate kingdoms. We meet up with again with a bunch of soldiers we met before plus some others. We see their doubts, trials, and tribulations they go through to pull off a seemingly impossible task set before them. Very compelling stuff as we get to know them intimately and feel the same sting of their losses.<br /><br />At the end the pieces that Erikson had set up over the past two books have been dashed across the board. Deaths come heavy and often at the end of this one, both of people and institutions. There are plenty of moments of levity mixed in (especially with Tehol and Bugg et. al.) but the course of whole peoples and civilizations are decided in this book. We still have the Crippled God lurking in the background, a strange, once thought extinct civilization returning, and plenty of other games played by the gods and ascendants. I adored this book and am eager to see what terrible things Erikson rains down upon his characters.<br /><br />And now, without further ado, some choice passages:<br /><br /><b>Most terrifying pinch ever</b>:<i> Karsa: And he is small - my people call you children. And that is all you truly are. Short-lived, stick limbed, with faces I want to pinch. The Edur are little different, just stretched out a bit.</i><br /><br /><b>Won't someone think of the (evilish) Children!?!?!?</b>:<i> But I always started to worry... about those evil minions, the victims of those bright heroes and their intractable righteousness. I mean, someone invades your hide-out, your cherished home, and of course you try to kill and eat them. Who wouldn't? there they were, nominally ugly and shifty-looking, busy with their own little lives, plaiting nooses or some such thing. Then shock! The alarms are raised! The intruders have somehow slipped their chains and death is a whirlwind in every corridor!</i><br /><br /><b>Always read the fine print</b>:<i> "Will you take it now?"<br />"I will - to break it on the forge where it was made."<br />"You said it could never be broken!"<br />"We're always saying things like that, pays the bills."</i><br /><br /><b>But who's on first?</b>:<i> "Well, that is why I sent for you - excuse me, but what is your name?"<br />"My name was discarded upon attaining my present tank within the Unified Sects of Cabal."<br />"I see, and what is that rank?"<br />"Senior assessor."<br />"Assessing what?"<br />"All matters requiring assessment. Is more explanation required?"</i><br /><br /><b>Fear the feathered and delicious ones</b>: <i>"You may find this amusing now, Bugg, but you are the one who will be sleeping down there. They'll</i> [newly acquired hens]<i> peck your eyes out, you know. Evil has been bred into them, generation after generation, until their tiny black bean brains are condensed knots of malice-"<br />"You display unexpected familiarity with hens, Master."<br />"I had a tutor who was a human version."</i><br /><br /><b>Metal makes for a terrible ruler (unless this is metaphorical...)</b>:<i> Leave a sword to rule an empire and the empire falls. Amidst war, amidst anarchy, amidst a torrent of blood and a sea of misery.</i><br /><br /><b>Damn it Udinaas, stop trying to be so genre savvy</b>:<i> Myths prefer manageable numbers, after all, and three always works best.</i><br /><br /><b>But would you say that to Justice's face?</b>:<i> That's the thing about Just Wars - they never end and never will because Justice is a weak god with too many names.</i><br /><br /><b>When a pissing contest turns real dark, real fast</b>:<i> "I was there when Redmask's sister killed herself."<br />"And I suckled at the tit of a K'Chain Che'Malle Matron. If tit is the right word."<br />"...I saw with my own eyes the great sea canoes. Upon the north shore. thousands upon thousands."<br />"These arrows were made by a dead man. Dead for a hundred thousand years, or more."<br />"I have seen skeletons running in the night - on this very plain."<br />"This body you see isn't mine. I stole it."<br />"I alone know the truth of the Bast Fulmar."<br />"This body's father was a dead man - he gasped his last breath as his seed was taken on a field of battle."<br />"The victory of long ago was in truth a defeat."<br />"This body grew strong on human meat."<br />"Redmask will betray us."<br />"This mouth waters as I look at you."</i><br /><br /><b>Why the gold standard is a TERRIBLE idea, even in fantasy settings or Keynes was right so shut your gob hole</b>:<i> "Why not just mint more coins and take the pressure</i> [of a currency shortage]<i> off?"<br />"We could, although it would not be easy. There is a fixed yield form the Imperial Mines and it is, of necessity, modest. And, unfortunately rather inflexible."</i><br /><br /><b>And why not be a buzz kill to end this review or echoes of Global Climate Change</b>:<i> It had not been imagined - by anyone - that an entire realm could die in such a manner. That the vicious acts of its inhabitants could destroy... everything. Worlds live on, had been the belief - the assumption - regardless of the activities of those who dwelt upon them. Torn flesh heals, the sky clears, and something new crawls from the briny muck.<br /><br />But not this time.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1102321942843210711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19778442-scott?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19778442-scott?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395860263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer267435278668510981">Brutal doesn't even begin to describe this novel. Some parts, especially dealing with the secret police of Lether, were nauseating and showed just the worst traits humans have to offer. <br/><br/>And then, of course, in contrast you have the friendship between Onrack and Trull and the camaraderie of the Malazan marines that I so love to read about<br/><br/>I was well and truly sucked into this book from the very beginning and stayed that way throughout. I never had that typical Malazan lull at the beginning. <br/><br/>Close </span>
  <span id="freeText267435278668510981" style="display:none">Brutal doesn't even begin to describe this novel. Some parts, especially dealing with the secret police of Lether, were nauseating and showed just the worst traits humans have to offer. <br /><br />And then, of course, in contrast you have the friendship between Onrack and Trull and the camaraderie of the Malazan marines that I so love to read about<br /><br />I was well and truly sucked into this book from the very beginning and stayed that way throughout. I never had that typical Malazan lull at the beginning. <br /><br />Close up there with being one of my favorites so far!<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wKFVQah2MHlZlQ5FdPXTsDoCgn++8tVhqIY+3rkO2JrqLXhcEWOoYKUgBrDwFmP2qoZmfT4jUib3AlDNkhNMXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rSOW+p9T3F49fsYlchqK+Iz4AI6C4MIolfhx8nOHYzqHr7vnJkZER8HLztD2+Tq+HHzkjAIxRW/KfB/hWJr3/Q==')})
  }
